        S2-J: Startup Tenant Validation Tests ù Pillar 2 + Pillar 3.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify that the application refuses to start
        (or visibly degrades) when tenant-critical infrastructure is missing or
        misconfigured.  They complement the existing test_startup_validation.py by
        focusing specifically on tenant isolation prerequisites.

        Expected Initial State:
            - test_startup_rejects_missing_jwt_secret_in_prod:     PASS
            - test_startup_rejects_weak_jwt_secret_in_prod:        FAIL (no length check)
            - test_startup_summary_reports_rls_status:              FAIL (no RLS in summary)
            - test_startup_validates_rls_prerequisites:             FAIL (no RLS validation)
            - test_degraded_redis_disables_rate_limiting:           PASS
            - test_degraded_redis_does_not_disable_auth:            PASS
        <Class TestJWTSecretValidation>
          Verify JWT secret is validated at startup.
          <Function test_startup_rejects_weak_jwt_secret_in_prod>
            Production startup must fail if JWT_SECRET is too short.

            A JWT secret shorter than 32 characters is brute-forceable.
            Expected initial state: FAIL ù no length validation exists.
          <Function test_startup_rejects_missing_jwt_secret_in_prod>
            Production startup must fail if JWT_SECRET is missing.
          <Function test_startup_rejects_default_jwt_secret_in_prod>
            Production must reject known default/test JWT secrets.
        <Class TestRLSPrerequisiteValidation>
          Verify startup validates RLS prerequisites.
          <Function test_startup_rejects_superuser_connection_in_prod>
            Production must warn/reject if connecting as PostgreSQL superuser.

            Superuser roles bypass all RLS policies, making tenant isolation
            completely ineffective.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù no superuser detection exists.
          <Function test_startup_validates_rls_prerequisites>
            Production startup must validate that the database supports RLS.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù no RLS prerequisite check exists.
        <Class TestDegradedDependencyBehavior>
          Verify correct behavior when dependencies are degraded.
          <Function test_degraded_audit_still_allows_startup>
            Missing audit sink should warn but not prevent startup.

            Audit is important but not a hard dependency ù the application
            should start with a warning, not crash.
          <Function test_degraded_redis_does_not_disable_auth>
            Missing Redis must NOT disable JWT authentication.

            Rate limiting can degrade gracefully, but authentication must
            never be optional ù even if Redis is down.

    <Dir state>
      <Module test_state_alignment.py>
        S1-A: State Enum Alignment Tests ù Production Approval Suite, Pillar 1.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify that the backend WorkflowStatus and
        WorkflowType enums are exactly aligned with the frontend TypeScript type
        definitions.  A mismatch means the UI will silently mishandle workflows in
        an unknown state ù this is a release-blocking defect.

        Expected Initial State:
            - test_backend_workflow_status_superset_of_frontend: FAIL
              (backend has ``INTERRUPTED`` which frontend lacks)
            - test_frontend_workflow_status_subset_of_backend:   FAIL
              (same root cause ù ``interrupted`` missing from frontend union)
            - test_workflow_type_enum_matches_frontend:          PASS or FAIL
            - test_no_duplicate_enum_aliases:                    Verify

        These tests parse source files directly (no runtime import of frontend code)
        so they run without Node.js and catch drift even when the two stacks are
        developed independently.
        <Class TestNoDuplicateEnumAliases>
          Verify that WorkflowType has no duplicate values (aliases).

          The backend currently has both ``WHITESPACE_ANALYSIS`` and
          ``WHITESPACE_ANALYSIS_WORKFLOW`` mapping to the same string value
          ``"whitespace_analysis"``.  While Python allows this, it creates
          confusion and potential routing bugs.
          <Function test_workflow_type_values_are_unique>
            Each WorkflowType member should map to a unique string value.
        <Class TestWorkflowStatusAlignment>
          Verify backend WorkflowStatus enum matches frontend TypeScript type.
          <Function test_exact_bidirectional_match>
            Frontend and backend must define exactly the same set of statuses.

            This is the combined gate ù if this passes, both directions are aligned.
          <Function test_frontend_workflow_status_subset_of_backend>
            Every frontend status must exist in the backend enum.

            Catches orphan frontend values that the backend would never produce,
            which would create dead UI branches.
          <Function test_backend_workflow_status_superset_of_frontend>
            Every backend status must exist in the frontend type.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù backend has ``interrupted`` which the
            frontend ``WorkflowStatus`` union does not include.  The fix is to add
            ``'interrupted'`` to the frontend type.
        <Class TestWorkflowTypeAlignment>
          Verify backend WorkflowType enum matches frontend workflow_type field.
          <Function test_backend_has_no_unreachable_workflow_types>
            Backend workflow types should be reachable from the frontend.

            Note: some backend types may be internal-only (e.g. document_ingestion).
            This test flags them for review ù they should be explicitly documented
            as internal if they are intentionally excluded from the frontend.
          <Function test_frontend_workflow_types_exist_in_backend>
            Every workflow type the frontend can create must be handled by the backend.

    <Dir config>
      <Module test_startup_validation.py>
        Startup and Control Hardening Tests (Suite 10).

        Verifies that production deployments fail fast when critical security
        controls are misconfigured, preventing silent degradation of tenant
        isolation, authentication, or audit capabilities.

        These tests catch the class of failures that tests often miss:
        - Missing Redis URL when Redis is required
        - Wildcard CORS in production
        - Missing JWT issuer/audience or signing config
        - Missing audit sink or required dependency
        - Startup summary reports active control mode correctly

        Test Strategy:
        - Mock environment variables to simulate misconfigurations
        - Attempt to initialize application components
        - Assert that startup fails with clear error messages
        - Verify control mode reporting is accurate
        <Class TestProductionAuditConfiguration>
          Verify audit sink is configured in production.
          <Coroutine test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_audit_sink>
            Production boot must fail if audit sink is not configured.

            Rationale: Missing audit sink means privileged operations are not
            logged, violating compliance requirements.
          <Coroutine test_dev_mode_allows_missing_audit_sink_with_warning>
            Development mode should warn but allow missing audit sink.
          <Coroutine test_prod_boot_fails_if_audit_sink_unreachable>
            Production boot must fail if audit sink is unreachable.

            Rationale: Unreachable audit sink means events will be lost,
            creating compliance gaps.
        <Class TestProductionJWTConfiguration>
          Verify JWT configuration is complete in production.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_jwt_audience>
            Production boot must fail if JWT_AUDIENCE is missing.

            Rationale: Missing audience allows tokens intended for other services
            to be accepted.
          <Function test_prod_accepts_valid_jwt_config>
            Production should accept properly configured JWT settings.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_jwt_issuer>
            Production boot must fail if JWT_ISSUER is missing.

            Rationale: Missing issuer allows tokens from any source to be accepted.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_weak_jwt_secret>
            Production boot must fail if JWT_SECRET is too short.

            Rationale: Weak secrets are vulnerable to brute force attacks.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_jwt_secret>
            Production boot must fail if JWT_SECRET is missing.

            Rationale: Missing JWT secret means tokens cannot be verified,
            allowing unauthenticated access.
        <Class TestProductionDatabaseConfiguration>
          Verify database is properly configured in production.
          <Function test_prod_boot_warns_with_unencrypted_database_connection>
            Production boot should warn if database connection is not encrypted.

            Rationale: Unencrypted connections expose tenant data in transit.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_sqlite_database>
            Production boot must fail if using SQLite.

            Rationale: SQLite does not support RLS or multi-tenant isolation.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_database_url>
            Production boot must fail if DATABASE_URL is missing.

            Rationale: Missing database URL means application cannot start.
        <Class TestNegativePathStartupScenarios>
          Test startup behavior under adverse conditions.
          <Function test_startup_validation_runs_before_server_start>
            Validation must run during import/init, not on first request.

            Rationale: Failing on first request means misconfigured app is running.
          <Function test_startup_with_all_controls_disabled>
            Startup must fail if all security controls are disabled in production.

            Rationale: This indicates a catastrophic misconfiguration.
          <Function test_conflicting_environment_variables>
            Startup must fail if environment variables conflict.

            Example: ENVIRONMENT=production but DEBUG=true
        <Class TestStartupControlModeReporting>
          Verify startup summary reports active control mode correctly.
          <Function test_startup_summary_reports_development_mode>
            Startup summary must clearly indicate development mode is active.
          <Function test_startup_summary_lists_degraded_controls>
            Startup summary must list any degraded or disabled controls.

            Rationale: Operators need to know which controls are not active.
          <Function test_startup_summary_reports_production_mode>
            Startup summary must clearly indicate production mode is active.

            Rationale: Operators need to verify production controls are enabled.
        <Class TestProductionCORSValidation>
          Verify CORS is properly restricted in production.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_wildcard_cors>
            Production boot must fail if CORS allows all origins.

            Rationale: Wildcard CORS (*) in production allows any website to
            make authenticated requests, bypassing same-origin policy.
          <Function test_prod_accepts_valid_https_cors_origins>
            Production should accept properly configured HTTPS CORS origins.
          <Function test_prod_boot_fails_with_http_cors_origin>
            Production boot must fail if CORS allows HTTP origins.

            Rationale: HTTP origins in production expose tokens to MITM attacks.
          <Function test_dev_mode_allows_wildcard_cors_with_warning>
            Development mode should warn but allow wildcard CORS.
        <Class TestProductionRedisRequirement>
          Verify Redis is required in production mode.
          <Coroutine test_dev_mode_allows_missing_redis_with_warning>
            Development mode should warn but not fail if Redis is missing.

            Rationale: Developers should be able to run locally without Redis,
            but must be warned about degraded behavior.
          <Coroutine test_prod_boot_fails_with_invalid_redis_url>
            Production boot must fail if REDIS_URL is malformed.

            Rationale: Malformed URL could cause silent fallback to in-memory cache,
            breaking tenant isolation in multi-worker deployments.
          <Coroutine test_prod_boot_fails_with_missing_redis_url>
            Production boot must fail if REDIS_URL is missing.

            Rationale: Rate limiting and cache isolation depend on Redis.
            Missing Redis in prod could silently disable tenant-scoped rate limits.

      <Module test_redis_failure.py>
        Chaos tests for Redis cache failure scenarios.

        Verifies system behavior when Redis becomes unavailable, including:
        - Cache operations do not return fake success
        - Errors are structured with appropriate codes
        - Tenant isolation is maintained
        - Degraded operation is explicit when fallback is allowed
        - Integrity-sensitive paths fail closed
        <Class TestRedisCacheFailure>
          Verify system behavior when Redis cache fails.
          <Coroutine test_redis_unavailable_fails_closed_for_integrity_sensitive_ops>
            When Redis is unavailable, integrity-sensitive operations fail closed.

            Operations that require cache consistency must fail rather than proceed
            with potentially stale data.
          <Coroutine test_redis_failure_does_not_bypass_tenant_isolation>
            Redis failure must not allow cross-tenant cache access.

            Security: When Redis fails, tenant A must not see tenant B's cached data.
            This is verified by ensuring no fallback to shared in-memory cache.
          <Coroutine test_redis_timeout_error_raises_or_degrades_explicitly>
            When Redis times out, the system must not fabricate a success response.

            Security: Timeout must not result in cached data being shared across tenants.
            Safety: The caller must know the operation failed or degraded.
          <Coroutine test_cache_get_failure_does_not_return_fabricated_data>
            When cache get fails, the system must not return fabricated cached data.

            A cache miss due to Redis failure must not be converted to a cache hit
            with fake/default data.
          <Coroutine test_redis_connection_error_raises_structured_error>
            When Redis connection fails, a structured error is returned.

            Security: The error must not expose internal Redis details.
            Safety: The error must indicate service unavailable, not fake success.
        <Class TestRedisDegradedMode>
          Verify explicit degraded mode when Redis fallback is allowed.
          <Coroutine test_degraded_read_through_does_not_expose_other_tenant_data>
            In degraded mode, cache fallback must not expose cross-tenant data.

            If cache is bypassed, the fallback must not use shared in-memory
            storage that could contain other tenants' data.
          <Coroutine test_redis_degraded_mode_is_explicit>
            When Redis degrades, the degradation must be explicit.

            If a service allows degraded operation without Redis, the response
            must indicate degraded status so callers can adjust behavior.
        <Class TestRedisPartialFailure>
          Verify behavior when Redis partially degrades (timeouts, slow responses).
          <Coroutine test_redis_slow_response_does_not_cause_cascade>
            Slow Redis responses must not cause cascading timeouts.

            The system must have circuit breaker or timeout patterns to prevent
            Redis slowness from affecting overall API availability.
          <Coroutine test_redis_connection_flapping_handled_gracefully>
            Flapping Redis connections must be handled without data corruption.

            If Redis connects/disconnects rapidly, operations must not result
            in partial writes or inconsistent state.

        <Module test_crm_webhook_auth_unit.py>
          CI-runnable unit tests for CRM webhook authentication logic.

          These tests verify the core authentication behavior without importing the
          full FastAPI route module (which requires langgraph, psycopg, etc.).

          Covers:
          - Per-tenant webhook token validation (constant-time comparison)
          - Missing token rejection (fail-closed)
          - Invalid token rejection
          - Global HMAC fallback (with warning)
          - HMAC signature mismatch (defense-in-depth)
          <Class TestWebhookTokenAuth>
            Test per-tenant webhook token authentication.
            <Coroutine test_valid_token_accepts>
              Webhook with correct per-tenant token is accepted.
            <Coroutine test_missing_token_rejects>
              Webhook with no token is rejected (fail-closed).
            <Coroutine test_invalid_token_rejects>
              Webhook with wrong per-tenant token is rejected with 401.
            <Coroutine test_no_token_configured_rejects>
              Integration with no webhook_token configured rejects all requests.
          <Class TestWebhookHMACAuth>
            Test HMAC signature verification (defense-in-depth).
            <Coroutine test_valid_token_and_valid_hmac_accepts>
              Both token and HMAC valid \u2192 accepted.
            <Coroutine test_global_hmac_fallback_rejects_bad_sig>
              No per-tenant token and bad global HMAC \u2192 rejected.
            <Coroutine test_global_hmac_fallback_accepts>
              No per-tenant token but valid global HMAC \u2192 accepted.
            <Coroutine test_valid_token_and_invalid_hmac_rejects>
              Valid token but bad HMAC \u2192 rejected (defense-in-depth).
          <Class TestWebhookConstantTimeComparison>
            Verify that token comparison uses constant-time hmac.compare_digest.
            <Coroutine test_empty_token_vs_empty_stored>
              Both empty should reject (fail-closed).
            <Coroutine test_timing_attack_resistance>
              Wrong-length token should still go through compare_digest, not early exit.
  <Package tests>
    <Package chaos>
      <Module test_database_failure.py>
        Chaos tests for database failure scenarios.

        Verifies system behavior when PostgreSQL becomes unavailable, including:
        - Session acquisition failures raise structured errors
        - Tenant context is not bypassed during failures
        - No fallback to raw DB connections occurs
        - Transaction integrity is maintained
        <Class TestDatabaseTransactionFailure>
          Verify behavior during database transaction failures.
          <Coroutine test_concurrent_transaction_isolation>
            Concurrent transactions must maintain isolation even under load.

            If one transaction fails, it must not affect other concurrent transactions
            or cause data leakage.
          <Coroutine test_transaction_rollback_on_failure>
            When transaction fails, partial changes must be rolled back.

            Integrity: Partial writes must not be visible to other transactions.
        <Class TestDatabaseConnectionFailure>
          Verify system behavior when database connection fails.
          <Coroutine test_database_unavailable_raises_structured_error>
            When database connection fails, a structured unavailable error is returned.

            Security: The error must not expose database credentials or internal details.
            Safety: The error must clearly indicate database unavailability.
          <Coroutine test_no_fallback_to_raw_db_connect>
            When async session fails, system must not fall back to raw sync connection.

            Security: Raw connections bypass tenant context setup and RLS policies.
            Safety: Must not create emergency workarounds that break isolation.
          <Coroutine test_session_acquisition_failure_fails_closed>
            When session cannot be acquired, the operation must fail closed.

            The operation must not proceed without a valid session, even if that
            would result in a denial of service.
          <Coroutine test_tenant_context_not_bypassed_during_db_failure>
            Database failure must not bypass tenant context validation.

            Security: If tenant context cannot be set due to DB failure,
            the operation must fail rather than proceed without tenant isolation.
        <Class TestTenantIsolationUnderFailure>
          Verify tenant isolation is maintained during database failures.
          <Coroutine test_tenant_context_cleared_on_session_return_to_pool>
            When session returns to pool, tenant context must be cleared.

            Security: Pool reuse must not retain previous tenant's context.
          <Coroutine test_rls_policy_enforced_even_when_query_fails>
            RLS policies must be enforced even if the underlying query fails.

            A query failure must not result in data being returned without RLS filtering.
        <Class TestDatabaseErrorContracts>
          Verify database errors follow structured error contracts.
          <Coroutine test_database_error_includes_error_code>
            Database errors must include standardized error codes.

            API consumers rely on error codes for retry logic and handling.
        <Class TestDatabaseDegradedModes>
          Verify behavior during partial database degradation.
          <Coroutine test_read_replica_failure_fails_over_explicitly>
            When read replica fails, failover must be explicit.

            The system must not silently switch to primary for reads without
            indicating the failover occurred.
          <Coroutine test_slow_query_timeout_does_not_leave_session_hanging>
            When query times out, the session must be properly closed.

            Resource leak prevention: Failed sessions must not accumulate in pools.
          <Coroutine test_connection_pool_exhaustion_fails_explicitly>
            When connection pool is exhausted, failure must be explicit.

            The system must not queue indefinitely or create unbounded connections.

          <Function test_future_issued_token_returns_401>

            Multiple Authorization headers are rejected.

            'Bearer' without space separator is rejected.

          <Function test_empty_authorization_header_returns_401>

          <Function test_malformed_jwt_structure_returns_401>

          <Function test_deleted_role_handling>

          Verify LLM safety mechanisms work even when LLM fails.
          <Coroutine test_prompt_guard_still_validates_on_llm_failure>
            When LLM is unavailable, prompt guard validation must still occur.

            Security: Dangerous prompts must be rejected even if LLM is down.
          <Coroutine test_output_guard_does_not_cache_failed_outputs>
            When LLM fails, partial outputs must not be cached for output guard bypass.

            Security: Failed/corrupted LLM outputs must not contaminate safety systems.
        <Class TestMultiProviderFallback>
          Verify behavior with multiple LLM providers when primary fails.
          <Coroutine test_fallback_provider_used_explicitly>
            When using fallback provider, the fallback usage must be explicit.

            If OpenAI fails and Anthropic is used as fallback, response should
            indicate which provider was used.
          <Coroutine test_all_providers_unavailable_fails_closed>
            When all LLM providers are unavailable, system fails closed.

            No cached responses or default content should be returned.
        <Class TestLLMProviderUnavailable>
          Verify behavior when LLM providers are unavailable.
          <Coroutine test_anthropic_api_error_returns_structured_failure>
            When Anthropic API returns error, system returns structured failure.
          <Coroutine test_llm_timeout_returns_explicit_timeout_error>
            When LLM call times out, explicit timeout error is returned.

            Caller must be able to distinguish timeout from other failures for retry logic.
          <Coroutine test_no_fabricated_output_on_llm_failure>
            When LLM fails, system must not return fabricated/generated output.

            Critical: The system must not attempt to "helpfully" generate a response
            when the LLM is unavailable.
          <Coroutine test_openai_api_error_returns_structured_failure>
            When OpenAI API returns error, system returns structured failure.

            Security: Error must not expose API keys or internal retry logic.
            Safety: Caller must know the LLM call failed.
        <Class TestLLMRateLimiting>
          Verify behavior when LLM rate limits are hit.
          <Coroutine test_rate_limit_does_not_cause_duplicate_requests>
            Rate limit errors must not cause automatic retries without backoff.

            Retry storms can worsen rate limit situations.
          <Coroutine test_rate_limit_error_includes_retry_after>
            When LLM rate limit is hit, error includes retry guidance.

            API design: Rate limit errors should include retry-after when available.
        <Class TestAgentWorkflowLLMFailure>
          Verify agent workflows handle LLM failures correctly.
          <Coroutine test_agent_workflow_returns_degraded_result_on_llm_failure>
            When LLM fails during agent execution, workflow returns degraded result.

            The result must explicitly indicate LLM was unavailable, not return
            partial or cached results as if they were fresh.
          <Coroutine test_tool_execution_fails_closed_when_llm_unavailable>
            Tool execution that requires LLM must fail closed when LLM unavailable.

            Tools that depend on LLM (generation, extraction) must not proceed
            with cached or default responses.
          <Coroutine test_correlation_id_preserved_on_llm_failure>
            When LLM fails, correlation/trace ID must be preserved.

            Observability: Failed requests must still be traceable through the system.
        <Class TestLLMCostTrackingFailure>
          Verify cost tracking handles LLM failures correctly.
          <Coroutine test_partial_response_cost_handling>
            When LLM returns partial response before failing, cost handling is explicit.

            If 500 tokens were generated before timeout, cost policy must be explicit.
          <Coroutine test_cost_not_recorded_on_llm_failure>
            When LLM call fails, no cost should be recorded.

            Financial integrity: Only successful calls should incur recorded costs.

        <Module test_neo4j_integration.py>
          Integration tests for Layer 3 Neo4j connectivity.

          These tests use ``testcontainers`` to spin up a real Neo4j 5.x instance and
          validate that:
          - The driver factory connects and verifies connectivity.
          - Schema initialisation creates all expected constraints and vector indexes.
          - ``Neo4jLoader`` can merge entity nodes using native Cypher (APOC-free path).
          - ``VectorStore`` can create a vector index and run a similarity query.
          - ``HybridSearch`` returns results without raising ``AttributeError``.
          - ``GraphRAGEngine`` returns a non-empty result dict when the driver is live.

          Run with::

              pytest tests/test_neo4j_integration.py -v -m integration

          Requirements (in addition to the project's dev extras)::

              pip install testcontainers[neo4j]

          The ``NEO4J_PASSWORD`` used inside the container is ``testpassword``.

          Docker Requirements:
              - Docker must be running for these tests to execute
              - Tests will be skipped if Docker is unavailable
              - Add to pytest.ini: markers = integration: marks tests as integration (deselect with '-m "not integration"')
          <Coroutine test_neo4j_loader_merge_capability_node>

            VectorStore.search() should return a list (possibly empty) without raising.
          <Coroutine test_neo4j_loader_merge_relationship>

      <Module test_export_tenant_access.py>
        S2-H: Export Tenant Access & Provenance Tests ù Pillar 2 + Pillar 5.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify that:
            1. Export endpoints require authentication (not optional context).
            2. Export storage paths are tenant-namespaced (no cross-tenant overwrites).
            3. Provenance manifests include tenant_id and are structurally complete.
            4. Export audit events are emitted with correct tenant context.

        Expected Initial State:
            - test_export_endpoint_requires_auth:       FAIL (uses get_optional_context)
            - test_export_storage_key_is_tenant_scoped: FAIL (no tenant prefix in key)
            - test_provenance_manifest_includes_tenant:  PASS
            - test_provenance_manifest_has_required_fields: PASS
        <Class TestExportEndpointAuth>
          Verify export endpoints require mandatory authentication.
          <Function test_export_endpoint_uses_tenant_scoped_db>
            Export endpoint must use get_db_from_context if it queries the DB.

            Even if the export reads from the workflow executor (Redis), the
            endpoint should use tenant-scoped DB for any audit writes.
          <Function test_export_endpoint_requires_auth_not_optional>
            GET /cases/{case_id}/export must use ``require_authenticated``,
            not ``get_optional_context``.

            Business case exports contain confidential financial projections,
            competitive analysis, and customer data.  Optional auth means an
            unauthenticated request could potentially access exports if the
            executor doesn't independently verify tenant ownership.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù uses get_optional_context.
        <Class TestExportStorageNamespacing>
          Verify export artifacts are stored in tenant-namespaced paths.
          <Function test_export_storage_key_includes_tenant_id>
            The S3 object key for exports must include the tenant_id.

            Without tenant namespacing, Tenant A could overwrite Tenant B's
            export if they share a case_id pattern, or a signed URL for
            Tenant A's export could be guessed by Tenant B.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù current code uses flat key structure.
          <Function test_export_storage_upload_requires_tenant_metadata>
            The upload_bytes function should accept tenant metadata.

            S3 object metadata should include tenant_id for audit trail
            and access control at the storage layer.
        <Class TestExportAuditTrail>
          Verify export operations emit audit events.
          <Function test_export_endpoint_emits_audit_event>
            The export endpoint must emit an audit event for compliance.

            Every export of confidential data must be logged with:
            - tenant_id
            - user_id
            - case_id
            - export format
            - timestamp
          <Function test_export_blocked_case_still_audited>
            Even blocked exports must be audited (attempted access logging).

            If a business case fails truth-gating, the export attempt must still
            be logged ù this is a compliance requirement.
        <Class TestProvenanceManifestStructure>

    <Package security>
      <Module test_rls_enforcement.py>
        S2-C: RLS Enforcement & Connection Pool Reset Tests ù Pillar 2.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify that:
            1. RLS migration scripts cover ALL tables with tenant_id columns.
            2. The ``get_db`` dependency does NOT set ``app.tenant_id`` (proving it
               bypasses RLS).
            3. The ``get_db_from_context`` dependency DOES set ``app.tenant_id``.
            4. Connection pool sessions are reset between requests (no tenant leakage).
            5. The ``db_session`` context manager validates tenant_id.

        Tests in this file are split into two categories:
            - **Static analysis** (no database required): Parse migration scripts and
              source code to verify structural invariants.
            - **Live database** (requires PostgreSQL): Execute actual SQL to verify RLS
              policies are enforced.  These are skipped locally if no DB is available,
              but hard-fail in CI.

        Expected Initial State:
            - test_all_tenant_tables_have_rls_policies: FAIL or PASS (depends on model scan)
            - test_get_db_does_not_set_tenant_context: PASS (confirms the vulnerability)
            - test_get_db_from_context_sets_tenant_id: PASS
            - test_rls_policy_uses_current_setting:    PASS
            - test_rls_null_tenant_id_allows_read:     FAIL (RLS policy allows NULL tenant_id)
        <Class TestRLSMigrationCoverage>
          Verify RLS policies cover all tables with tenant_id columns.
          <Function test_all_tenant_tables_have_rls_policies>
            Every model with tenant_id must have a corresponding RLS policy.

            This test compares the set of tables declared in RLS migration scripts
            against the set of SQLAlchemy models that have a tenant_id column.
          <Function test_rls_tables_list_is_not_empty>
            Sanity check: we should find at least 8 tables with RLS policies.
        <Class TestConnectionPoolReset>
          Verify that database sessions are properly reset between requests.

          If ``app.tenant_id`` persists across connection pool reuse, Tenant A's
          context could leak into Tenant B's request.
          <Function test_session_uses_set_local_not_set>
            Database module must use ``SET LOCAL`` (transaction-scoped), not
            ``SET`` (session-scoped).

            ``SET LOCAL`` automatically resets when the transaction ends.
            ``SET`` persists across the connection's lifetime, which means
            connection pool reuse would leak tenant context.
          <Function test_no_raw_set_without_local>
            No ``SET app.tenant_id`` (without LOCAL) should appear anywhere.
          <Function test_session_commits_or_rollbacks>
            Every session context manager must have both commit and rollback paths.

            If a session is returned to the pool without commit/rollback, the
            ``SET LOCAL`` may persist in some database drivers.
        <Class TestRLSPolicyStructure>
          Verify RLS policies use the correct PostgreSQL patterns.
          <Function test_rls_null_tenant_id_policy_is_safe>
            RLS policies must NOT allow rows with NULL tenant_id to be visible
            to all tenants.

            The current policy has ``tenant_id IS NULL OR ...`` which means rows
            without a tenant_id are visible to everyone.  This is a data leak risk
            if any code path accidentally inserts rows without setting tenant_id.

            This test understands migration ordering: if a later migration fixes
            the NULL pattern for the same tables, the earlier migration is not
            flagged (the later one supersedes it at runtime).

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù current policy allows NULL.
          <Function test_rls_policy_uses_current_setting>
            RLS policies must use ``current_setting('app.tenant_id', true)``.
          <Function test_rls_force_enabled>
            RLS must be FORCE enabled (applies even to table owners).
        <Class TestDatabaseModuleStructure>
          Verify the L4 database module enforces tenant context correctly.
          <Function test_get_db_from_context_sets_tenant_id>
            Verify ``get_db_from_context`` sets ``app.tenant_id`` via SET LOCAL.
          <Function test_get_db_sets_empty_tenant_context>
            Confirm that ``get_db`` sets ``app.tenant_id`` to empty string.

            get_db sets app.tenant_id = '' which is the admin bypass pattern.
            This means it relies on PostgreSQL admin_role to access data,
            bypassing RLS entirely.  This is acceptable for health checks but
            dangerous for business endpoints ù which is why S2-A and S2-B tests
            gate on migrating all callers to get_db_from_context.
          <Function test_get_db_from_context_validates_tenant_id>
            get_db_from_context must call validate_tenant_id before using it.
          <Function test_validate_tenant_id_exists>
            The database module must have a validate_tenant_id function.
    <Package contract>
      <Module test_journey_contracts.py>
        Journey-Paired Backend Contract Tests

        Each test in this module corresponds to a canonical user journey defined in
        frontend/e2e/journeys/. While the Playwright journey tests verify UI behavior,
        these tests verify that the backend APIs return correct data shapes, enforce
        tenant isolation, and maintain provenance integrity.

        Together, they prevent the failure mode: "UI passes but platform behavior is wrong."

        Environment Variables:
            LAYER1_API_URL: Layer 1 Ingestion API (default: http://localhost:8001)
            LAYER3_API_URL: Layer 3 Knowledge API (default: http://localhost:8003)
            LAYER4_API_URL: Layer 4 Agents API (default: http://localhost:8004)
            LAYER5_API_URL: Layer 5 Ground Truth API (default: http://localhost:8005)
            CONTRACT_TEST_MODE: Set to 'mock' for CI without running services

        Usage:
            # Against live services:
            pytest tests/contract/test_journey_contracts.py -v

            # In mock mode (CI):
            CONTRACT_TEST_MODE=mock pytest tests/contract/test_journey_contracts.py -v
        <Class TestJourney2IntelligenceContract>

        Validates that the system properly validates and sanitizes all input

        - Unsafe string sanitization

        <Class TestPayloadSizeLimits>
          Verify oversized payload rejection (DoS prevention).

          NOTE: These tests document production gaps. Actual implementation must:
          1. Configure FastAPI request size limits (P1)
          2. Add JSON depth validation middleware (P2)
          3. Add array size limits in Pydantic schemas (P2)

          See: SECURITY.md for production hardening checklist.
          <Function test_payload_size_limit_returns_413>
            Oversized request bodies are rejected at the edge with HTTP 413.
          <Function test_json_depth_limit_enforced>

          Verify content type validation.

            Negative: Requests with unexpected content types should be rejected.

            Prevents confusion attacks with wrong content types.
        <Class TestUnknownFieldHandling>
          Verify unknown field rejection or stripping policy.
          <Function test_unknown_fields_rejected_with_strict_schema>
            Negative: Unknown fields should be rejected when strict validation enabled.

            Prevents data pollution and schema evolution attacks.
          <Function test_unknown_fields_stripped_with_permissive_schema>
            Positive: When configured, unknown fields are silently stripped.

            This is a valid policy choice but should be intentional.
        <Class TestEnumAndStateValidation>

            Prevents data pollution with unexpected status values.
        <Class TestUnsafeStringSanitization>
          Verify unsafe string content is sanitized.

          NOTE: These tests document security gaps. Production implementation must:
          1. Add XSS sanitization middleware ( bleach/html-sanitizer )

      <Module test_tenant_context_contract.py>
        S2-A: Tenant Context Contract Tests ù Production Approval Suite, Pillar 2.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify structural invariants about how every
        route in the platform resolves tenant identity.  They parse source code and
        inspect FastAPI dependency graphs ù no running database required.

        Key invariants tested:
            1. No L4 route uses the deprecated ``get_db`` dependency (must use
               ``get_db_from_context`` which enforces RLS via tenant_id).
            2. No route uses ``get_optional_context`` for write/mutation endpoints.
            3. GovernanceMiddleware always resets the ContextVar at request start.
            4. RequestContext.tenant_id is always a UUID (never a raw string).
            5. The ``require_authenticated`` dependency raises 401 when context is None.

        Expected Initial State:
            - test_no_l4_routes_use_deprecated_get_db:  FAIL (9 endpoints in accounts.py)
            - test_no_write_routes_use_optional_context: FAIL (export_business_case)
            - test_governance_middleware_resets_context:  PASS
            - test_require_authenticated_rejects_none:   PASS
            - test_request_context_tenant_id_is_uuid:    PASS
        <Class TestNoOptionalContextOnWriteRoutes>
          Write/mutation endpoints must use ``require_authenticated``, not
          ``get_optional_context``.

          ``get_optional_context`` returns ``None`` when no auth is present, which
          means the endpoint handler must manually check ù and if it forgets, the
          mutation proceeds without tenant scoping.
          <Function test_no_write_routes_use_optional_context>
            Scan all L4 route files for write endpoints using get_optional_context.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù analysis.py export_business_case uses
            get_optional_context on a POST endpoint.
        <Class TestGovernanceMiddlewareContextReset>
          GovernanceMiddleware must reset the ContextVar at the start of every
          request to prevent tenant context leakage between requests sharing the
          same ASGI worker.
          <Function test_dispatch_resets_context_in_finally>
            Verify the dispatch method resets context in a finally block.

            Even if the request handler raises an exception, the context must be
            cleaned up to prevent leakage to the next request.
          <Function test_dispatch_resets_context_at_start>
            Verify the dispatch method sets context to None before resolution.
        <Class TestRequestContextIntegrity>
          Verify RequestContext enforces type safety on tenant_id.
          <Function test_request_context_accepts_uuid>
            RequestContext.tenant_id must accept UUID objects.
          <Function test_context_var_isolation>
            ContextVar must isolate between set/reset cycles.
          <Function test_require_context_raises_when_none>
            require_context() must raise RuntimeError when no context is set.
        <Class TestNoDeprecatedGetDb>
          Every L4 route must use ``get_db_from_context``, never bare ``get_db``.

          ``get_db`` creates a database session without setting ``app.tenant_id``,
          which means RLS policies are not enforced.  This is the single most
          critical tenant isolation defect class.
          <Function test_get_db_from_context_requires_tenant_id>
            Verify ``get_db_from_context`` rejects requests without tenant context.

            This is a unit test of the dependency function itself.
          <Function test_no_l4_routes_use_deprecated_get_db>
            Scan all L4 route files for ``Depends(get_db)`` usage.

            Expected initial state: FAIL ù accounts.py has 9 endpoints using get_db.
        <Class TestImportConsistency>
          Verify that route files import from the correct identity module.
          <Function test_l4_routes_import_shared_identity>
            L4 route files that use auth must import from shared.identity, not
            from the deprecated layer4-agents/src/tenant/ package.
          <Function test_all_route_files_that_use_db_import_it>
            Route files using Depends(get_db) or Depends(get_db_from_context)
            must have a matching import statement.
      <Module test_cross_tenant_api.py>
        S2-B: Cross-Tenant API Isolation Tests ù Production Approval Suite, Pillar 2.

        Ship/No-Ship Gate: These tests verify that Tenant A's JWT cannot read, modify,
        or delete resources belonging to Tenant B.  They exercise the actual FastAPI
        route handlers through ``TestClient`` with signed JWTs.

        Because the L4 app requires PostgreSQL, Redis, and checkpoint infrastructure
        at startup, these tests use a **lightweight mock app** that mirrors the real
        route registration and GovernanceMiddleware wiring but stubs out external
        dependencies.  This lets us test the auth/tenant enforcement layer in isolation.

        Expected Initial State:
            - Tests targeting accounts routes: FAIL (accounts.py uses get_db, no tenant scoping)
            - Tests targeting workflow routes:  PASS (workflows.py uses require_authenticated)
            - Tests targeting signal routes:    PASS (signals.py uses require_authenticated)

        The tests that FAIL prove the RLS bypass is exploitable at the HTTP layer.
        When the accounts routes are migrated to get_db_from_context, these tests
        will pass.

    <Package k8s>
      <Module test_routing_check.py>
        Unit tests for `scripts/ci/k8s_routing_check.py`.

        These tests exercise the gate's behaviour against minimal synthetic renders so
        that future changes to the gate cannot silently weaken its guarantees:

          - Mutual exclusivity of routing kinds per axis.
          - Sentinel-survival detection (`__HOST__`, `__API_HOST__`).
          - Per-listener bucket-swap detection (an `https-api` listener that carries
            the frontend host must fail).
          - Hostname mismatch against `routing-host` ConfigMap.
          - Missing `routing-host` ConfigMap.
          - Backend Service-existence.
          - Routing stack importing `../../base`.

        The gate is invoked as a subprocess so we cover the real CLI surface; this
        matches the way CI runs it.
        <Function test_gate_detects_sentinel_survival>
          A sentinel left in the rendered output fails the gate.
        <Function test_gate_detects_forbidden_kind_for_axis>
          A Gateway API resource leaking into an nginx-axis render fails mutex.
        <Function test_gate_detects_hostname_mismatch>
          A host that is neither `host` nor `apiHost` fails consistency.
        <Function test_gate_tolerates_comments_about_base>
          A comment mentioning `../../base` does not trip the base-import rule.

          Regression test: an earlier implementation grepped raw text and tripped
          on documentation comments. The current implementation parses YAML.
        <Function test_gate_detects_routing_stack_importing_base>
          Routing stacks must not import `../../base`.
        <Function test_gate_accepts_valid_nginx_render>
          A clean nginx-axis render passes all five gates.
        <Function test_gate_detects_missing_routing_host_configmap>
          A render that omits the routing-host ConfigMap fails.
        <Function test_gate_detects_listener_bucket_swap>
          An `https-api` listener that carries the frontend host must fail.

          This is the regression test for the P1 weakness identified during
          refinement: previously the gate dumped every listener host into both
          buckets, so a swap was invisible. After the refactor, listener.name
          classifies each host into its expected bucket and the swap is caught.
        <Function test_gate_detects_unknown_backend_service>
          A backend Service ref that does not exist in the render fails.

      <Module test_secrets_protection.py>
        P1: Secrets Protection Tests ù Production Assurance Suite.

        Validates that sensitive data (API keys, passwords, JWT tokens, credentials)
        is never exposed in logs, error responses, or audit trails.

        These tests verify ACTUAL current behavior, not document future gaps.
        For documented security gaps, see: .windsurf/plans/security-gaps.md
        <Class TestHeaderSanitization>
          Verify sensitive headers are handled safely.
          <Function test_api_key_header_is_sanitized>
            X-API-Key headers should be redacted in logs.
          <Function test_authorization_header_is_sanitized>
            Authorization headers should not appear in logs or traces.
        <Class TestSecretsNotInPlaintextLogs>
          Verify secrets never appear in plaintext log output.
          <Function test_api_key_prefix_not_logged_in_plaintext>
            API keys with 'vf_' prefix must not appear in plaintext logs.
          <Function test_password_not_logged>
            Document P1 requirement: Passwords must never appear in any log output.

            Passwords are the most sensitive credential type.
            Production must sanitize authentication payloads before logging.
          <Function test_jwt_token_not_logged_in_plaintext>
            Document P1 requirement: Full JWT tokens must not appear in plaintext logs.

            JWTs contain sensitive claims and could be reused if leaked.
            Production must implement request logging middleware that redacts
            Authorization headers before writing to logs.
          <Function test_database_connection_string_not_logged>
            Document P1 requirement: Database credentials in connection strings must be redacted.

            Connection strings often contain embedded passwords.
            Production must parse and redact credentials from logged connection strings.
        <Class TestErrorResponseSanitization>
          Verify error responses don't expose secrets.
          <Function test_authentication_errors_use_generic_messages>
            Auth errors must use generic messages without credential hints.
          <Function test_validation_errors_sanitize_sensitive_fields>
            Validation errors must not echo sensitive field values.
        <Class TestSecretHashingBehavior>
          Verify secret hashing helper works correctly.
          <Function test_hash_is_one_way>
            Hash should not be reversible to original secret.
          <Function test_different_secrets_produce_different_hashes>
            Different secrets should produce different hashes.
          <Function test_hash_is_deterministic>
            Same secret should always produce same hash.

        Chaos tests for external API and enrichment dependency failures.

        Verifies system behavior when external enrichment sources, crawlers, or

        - Ingestion/enrichment client failures don't crash workflows

        - Retry policy and error classification are applied
        - Tenant isolation is maintained

            External dependency errors must be classified by severity.

            P0: Data loss, security breach
            P1: Feature degraded
            P2: Monitoring/alerting only
        <Class TestTenantIsolationUnderExternalFailure>
          Verify tenant isolation when external dependencies fail.
          <Coroutine test_external_api_credentials_not_leaked_on_failure>
            When external API fails, credentials must not appear in error messages.

            Security: API keys, tokens must not be exposed in logs or error responses.
          <Coroutine test_external_cache_failure_does_not_expose_cross_tenant_data>
            When external cache (Redis/CDN) fails, tenant isolation must be maintained.

            Fallback to shared storage must not expose cross-tenant data.
        <Class TestRetryPolicyApplication>
          Verify retry policies are applied correctly.
          <Coroutine test_retry_backoff_prevents_thundering_herd>
            Retry backoff must prevent thundering herd when service recovers.

            Security: Randomized exponential backoff prevents synchronized retries.
          <Coroutine test_no_retry_on_permanent_failures>
            Permanent failures (400, 404) must not trigger retry.

            Efficiency: Don't waste resources on non-retriable errors.
          <Coroutine test_retry_policy_applied_to_transient_failures>
            Transient failures (503, timeout) trigger retry with backoff.

            Retry must not be applied to permanent failures (404, 400).
        <Class TestCrawlerDependencyFailure>
          Verify crawler behavior when dependencies fail.
          <Coroutine test_crawler_handles_robots_txt_fetch_failure>
            When robots.txt fetch fails, crawler must make safe assumption.

            Compliance: If robots.txt is unreachable, assume disallow-all (conservative).
          <Coroutine test_crawler_handles_target_site_unavailable>
            When target site is unreachable, error must be explicit.

            The failure must be distinguished from successful crawl with no data.
          <Coroutine test_crawler_quality_gate_still_enforced_under_failure>
            When crawling fails, quality gates must still be enforced.

            Low-quality data must not slip through because of failure conditions.
        <Class TestExternalAPIFailure>
          Verify behavior when external APIs fail.
          <Coroutine test_partial_state_is_explicit>
            When external dependency fails, partial state must be explicitly indicated.

            The caller must know that the result is incomplete.
          <Coroutine test_external_api_connection_error_fails_explicitly>
            When external API is unreachable, error is explicit and structured.

            Security: Error must not expose internal network details.
            Safety: Caller must know the external dependency failed.
          <Coroutine test_external_api_timeout_handled_gracefully>
            When external API times out, workflow continues with explicit degraded state.

            The workflow must not crash; it must continue with the degradation noted.
          <Coroutine test_workflow_does_not_crash_on_external_failure>
            External API failure must not crash the entire workflow.

            Resilience: Partial failures should be isolated.
        <Class TestCircuitBreakerPattern>
